# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

55-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive answer documenting all the Java source files that implement the inter-broker replication protocol in apache/kafka. Here's what I found:

## Summary

I identified **21 key files** implementing the inter-broker replication protocol components:

### Core Replication Components:
- **ReplicaFetcherThread** - Follower's fetching thread from leader
- **AbstractFetcherThread** - Base framework for all fetcher threads
- **ReplicaFetcherManager** - Manages fetcher thread lifecycle
- **RemoteLeaderEndPoint & LocalLeaderEndPoint** - Abstractions for leader communication

### Epoch Management:
- **LeaderEpochFileCache** - Maps leader epochs to offsets (critical for safe truncation after leader elections)
- **LogLoader** - Recovers epoch cache during startup

### Log Management:
- **UnifiedLog** - Main log storage with logStartOffset tracking
- **LogOffsetMetadata**, **LogOffsetSnapshot**, **LoadedLogOffsets** - Offset tracking structures
- **LogSegment** - Individual log segments with recovery logic
- **ProducerStateManager** - Transactional state during replication

### ISR Management:
- **Partition** - Contains maybeShrinkIsr() and maybeExpandIsr() logic
- **LeaderAndIsr** - Represents ISR state with leader epoch
- **AlterPartitionManager** - Coordinates ISR changes with controller
- **BrokersToIsrs** - Controller-side ISR tracking

The answer file includes detailed descriptions of how these components work together to ensure data consistency through epoch-based truncation, ISR management for durability, and logStartOffset tracking for cleanup safety.

It extends AbstractFetcherThread and implements the processPartitionData method to handle incoming data, managing high watermark updates and log start offset increments via LogStartOffsetIncrementReason.LeaderOffsetIncremented.\\n\\n2. **AbstractFetcherThread** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/AbstractFetcherThread.scala): The base class for all fetcher threads, providing the framework for fetching and truncation logic. It uses OffsetForLeaderEpoch requests to determine the correct truncation point based on leader epochs.\\n\\n3. **ReplicaFetcherManager** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ReplicaFetcherManager.scala): Manages the creation and lifecycle of ReplicaFetcherThread instances, one per leader broker.\\n\\n4. **LeaderEpochFileCache** (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/epoch/LeaderEpochFileCache.java): A critical component that maintains the mapping of leader epochs to their start offsets. It uses a TreeMap to store epoch entries and persists them to a checkpoint file. This enables replicas to truncate at the correct offset when a new leader is elected.\\n\\n5. **UnifiedLog** (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/UnifiedLog.java): The main log storage class that manages logStartOffset and tracks log end offset. Used in LeaderAndIsrRequest to propagate ISR information from controller to brokers.\\n\\n9. **AlterPartitionManager** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/AlterPartitionManager.scala): Coordinates ISR changes with the controller by sending AlterPartitionRequest and handling AlterPartitionResponse, managing pending ISR updates (PendingExpandIsr and PendingShrinkIsr).\\n\\n10. **BrokersToIsrs** (metadata/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/controller/BrokersToIsrs.java): Controller-side data structure that tracks which brokers are in the ISR for each partition, enabling ISR-aware leader election.\\n\\n11. **ProducerStateManager** (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/ProducerStateManager.java): Maintains producer transaction state during replication, recovered alongside log data via LogLoader.\\n\\n12. **RemoteLeaderEndPoint** and **LocalLeaderEndPoint** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/RemoteLeaderEndPoint.scala, core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/LocalLeaderEndPoint.scala): Abstractions for fetching from leader, supporting both remote and local leaders. They handle OffsetsForLeaderEpoch requests for truncation point determination.\\n\\n13. **RemoteLogManager** (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/log/remote/storage/RemoteLogManager.java): Manages tiered storage integration with the replication protocol, coordinating epoch-based offset searches in remote tiers.\\n\\nThe protocol ensures data consistency through multiple mechanisms: epoch-based truncation prevents divergence after leader elections, ISR management ensures write durability with min.insync.replicas, and logStartOffset tracking enables log cleanup while maintaining replication safety. \"BrokersToIsrs\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"The inter-broker replication protocol in Apache Kafka is implemented through several key components working together:\\n\\n1. **ReplicaFetcherThread** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ReplicaFetcherThread.scala): The main thread responsible for followers fetching data from the leader. It extends AbstractFetcherThread and implements the processPartitionData method to handle incoming data, managing high watermark updates and log start offset increments via LogStartOffsetIncrementReason.LeaderOffsetIncremented.\\n\\n2. **AbstractFetcherThread** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/AbstractFetcherThread.scala): The base class for all fetcher threads, providing the framework for fetching and truncation logic. It uses OffsetForLeaderEpoch requests to determine the correct truncation point based on leader epochs.\\n\\n3. **ReplicaFetcherManager** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ReplicaFetcherManager.scala): Manages the creation and lifecycle of ReplicaFetcherThread instances, one per leader broker.\\n\\n4. **LeaderEpochFileCache** (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/epoch/LeaderEpochFileCache.java): A critical component that maintains the mapping of leader epochs to their start offsets. It uses a TreeMap to store epoch entries and persists them to a checkpoint file. This enables replicas to truncate at the correct offset when a new leader is elected.\\n\\n5. **UnifiedLog** (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/UnifiedLog.java): The main log storage class that manages logStartOffset and tracks log end offset. It coordinates with LeaderEpochFileCache for epoch-based truncation and maintains high watermarks. The logStartOffset field is volatile and tracks the oldest offset available.\\n\\n6. **LogStartOffset Tracking**: Implemented through several related classes:\\n   - LogOffsetMetadata: Represents an offset with its physical file position\\n   - LogOffsetSnapshot: Contains snapshots of logStartOffset, logEndOffset, and highWatermark atomically\\n   - LoadedLogOffsets: Contains the logStartOffset and recoveryPoint loaded from checkpoint\\n\\n7. **ISR (In-Sync Replica) Management** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/cluster/Partition.scala): The Partition class implements ISR shrinking and expansion:\\n   - maybeShrinkIsr(): Removes replicas that have fallen too far behind from the ISR\\n   - maybeExpandIsr(): Adds replicas that have caught up back to the ISR\\n   - AlterPartitionListener interface with markIsrShrink() and markIsrExpand() methods to notify the controller of ISR changes\\n\\n8. **ISR State Representation** (metadata/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/metadata/LeaderAndIsr.java): Contains the leader, leader epoch, ISR list, and partition epoch. Used in LeaderAndIsrRequest to propagate ISR information from controller to brokers.\\n\\n9. **AlterPartitionManager** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/AlterPartitionManager.scala): Coordinates ISR changes with the controller by sending AlterPartitionRequest and handling AlterPartitionResponse, managing pending ISR updates (PendingExpandIsr and PendingShrinkIsr).\\n\\n10. **BrokersToIsrs** (metadata/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/controller/BrokersToIsrs.java): Controller-side data structure that tracks which brokers are in the ISR for each partition, enabling ISR-aware leader election.\\n\\n11. **ProducerStateManager** (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/ProducerStateManager.java): Maintains producer transaction state during replication, recovered alongside log data via LogLoader.\\n\\n12. **RemoteLeaderEndPoint** and **LocalLeaderEndPoint** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/RemoteLeaderEndPoint.scala, core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/LocalLeaderEndPoint.scala): Abstractions for fetching from leader, supporting both remote and local leaders. They handle OffsetsForLeaderEpoch requests for truncation point determination.\\n\\n13. **RemoteLogManager** (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/log/remote/storage/RemoteLogManager.java): Manages tiered storage integration with the replication protocol, coordinating epoch-based offset searches in remote tiers.\\n\\nThe protocol ensures data consistency through multiple mechanisms: epoch-based truncation prevents divergence after leader elections, ISR management ensures write durability with min.insync.replicas, and logStartOffset tracking enables log cleanup while maintaining replication safety. LogLoader (storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/LogLoader.java) recovers both LeaderEpochFileCache and ProducerStateManager during broker startup, maintaining protocol correctness across restarts.\"\n}\n",
